<div id="review_3394077367" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3394077367" />
    <a title="Bruce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3996101-bruce"><img alt="Bruce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591156662p2/3996101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3394077367?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bruce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bruce" href="/user/show/3996101-bruce">Bruce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8612458-makers">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3394077367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14495340314832416172">It seems that people either love this book or hate this book. No middle ground.<br/><br/>One of the reasons that people tend to dislike Makers is that it seems to advocate a socio-communal social structure where people are basically good and if you just get the lawyers out of the way, everything will work out. However, even the author doesn't seem to believe this worldview very strongly because choices have consequences and the relationships between the best and nicest people tend to decay like a rotten t</span>
  <span id="freeText14495340314832416172" style="display:none">It seems that people either love this book or hate this book. No middle ground.<br /><br />One of the reasons that people tend to dislike Makers is that it seems to advocate a socio-communal social structure where people are basically good and if you just get the lawyers out of the way, everything will work out. However, even the author doesn't seem to believe this worldview very strongly because choices have consequences and the relationships between the best and nicest people tend to decay like a rotten tooth ("all we do is magnify each other's flaws").<br /><br />I gave it 5 stars for a number of reasons.<br /><br />The author wrote this book just 10 years ago (hello 2020 and COVID19) yet he pressed the fabric of the technology just a bit further into the future than where we are today. At that time, 3D printers were relatively primitive, the goop expensive and touchy, and yet he saw where he would lead. I built a kit today with a micro-controller and a servo motor; the author saw a world where these parts were so readily available, so open, and so mass-produced that you could take old toys apart, re-assemble them, re-flash the firmware and re-use the tech for entire different purposes at a scale that the original innovators never conceived.<br /><br />Social media in "Makers" is even more pervasive than it is today. Heaven help us if Facebook embeds itself any further into our lives (and people willingly give up the last vestiges of their privacy without a thought). I do wish that the complex filtering and reporting in social media, as described in the book, existed today.<br /><br />Credit cards have "pay patches" in the surfaces of tables in restaurants and bars. Our "tap to pay" with our phones or cards is almost there.<br /><br />Disneyland, in the book, has severed itself from Walt Disney's vision and are simply a group of corporate profit centers. It's still the Happiest Place on Earth, but we accept a far lower standard for happiness. And, like Facebook, Disney (in the book) wants to extend their reach in every home in America (and beyond).<br /><br />I follow the author on Twitter. He may only write several hundred words a day but they are quality words.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14495340314832416172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/7125076-rachel">Rachel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125076-rachel?shelf=sf">sf</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3431646597" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12819377325056754916">I should read Cory Doctorow's books when they are new. This suffered from being set in a future that is mostly past now. (One tiny detail he got wrong: Jimmy Carter is still very much alive.) I enjoyed reading it, a lot - it has Doctorow's typical one-of-a-kind geeky characters and madcap tech. <br/><br/>But some things were cringeworthy, like calling people who took a treatment to reverse obesity "fatkins," and other things were too inconsistent, like if that obesity treatment were possible, the medical/</span>
  <span id="freeText12819377325056754916" style="display:none">I should read Cory Doctorow's books when they are new. This suffered from being set in a future that is mostly past now. (One tiny detail he got wrong: Jimmy Carter is still very much alive.) I enjoyed reading it, a lot - it has Doctorow's typical one-of-a-kind geeky characters and madcap tech. <br /><br />But some things were cringeworthy, like calling people who took a treatment to reverse obesity "fatkins," and other things were too inconsistent, like if that obesity treatment were possible, the medical/body mod fields would have more revolutionary changes. And more related to the main plot, if 3D printers were readily available and could do all the things they did in the book, the culture would be much more affected.<br /><br />I also was not fond of the ending, nor of the epilogue 15 years later. Seemed like the world was pretty much the same old place. Given what happened previously in the book, I'd think not.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2346336152" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2346336152" />
    <a title="Aaron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57377684-aaron"><img alt="Aaron" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2346336152?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aaron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aaron" href="/user/show/57377684-aaron">Aaron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2346336152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5868207838099087785">So this book was actually pretty good in terms of writing. Normally I’d rate this book the same as I rate his other books, a solid four, but I was pretty turned off by what seemed like a lot of, and this is the only term I know for it, fat shaming. It was supposed to be a book about ideas and technology, how a future non centralized economy could work, but there was almost a fixation on putting down overweight people. Very out of place with the tone of the book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16360252246232933188" style="display:none">I thought this book was just fine. I have enjoyed other novels by Doctorow more than this but it had some cool ideas, the idea of repurposing technology and obsolete products a good one. I really believe that the mining of the future will be in our waist dump sights - though not exactly what is going on here, it's close.<br /><br />The sub-idea of obesity in north America caused by such establishments as IHOP was also an interesting addition to the whole (I learned today, as a matter of fact, that we have four of these in the whole of Canada, which reminded me I had yet to write a review for this novel).<br /><br />Good characters, compelling story, an overall fine and well worth read.</span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_294941'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/294941.Cybernetics"><img alt="Cybernetics: or the Control and Communication in the Animal and the Machine" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1347245279l/294941._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+5f+Z27jIHwbAyjlGzWdVWAZvDLp6RMWVpErWl89xXRY3WsbbhwQPkr2Pw5q3EHuOM+4VNClJO7Dt7F7qQhpug==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

In Malcolm and Me, Reed, acclaimed author of such classic novels as Mumbo Jumbo and winner of a MacArthur &quot;Genius&quot; Fellowship, reveals a side of Malcolm X the public has never seen before, while exploring how the civil rights firebrand influenced his own views on working, living, speaking out, and left a mark on generations of artists and activists.\n\nMalcolm X was one of the most influential human rights activists in history and his views on race, religion, and fighting back changed America and the world. Reed gives us a clear-eyed view of what the man was really like—beyond the headlines and the myth-making. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15649677941057071107">Cory Doctorow is a science fiction author, activist, journalist and blogger — the co-editor of <a href='http://www.boingboing.net' rel='nofollow noopener'>Boing Boing</a> and the author of the YA graphic novel <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20575446._In_Real_Life' title=' In Real Life' rel='nofollow noopener'> In Real Life</a>,</i> the nonfiction business book <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20763766._Information_Doesn_t_Want_To_Be_Free' title=' Information Doesn’t Want To Be Free' rel='nofollow noopener'> Information Doesn’t Want To Be Free</a>,</i> and young adult novels like <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6278041._Homeland' title=' Homeland' rel='nofollow noopener'> Homeland</a>,</i> <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13539171._Pirate_Cinema' title=' Pirate Cinema' rel='nofollow noopener'> Pirate Cinema</a>,</i> and <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/954674._Little_Brother' title=' Little Brother' rel='nofollow noopener'> Little Brother</a>
</i> and novels for adults like <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13538762._Rapture_Of_The_Nerds' title=' Rapture Of The Nerds' rel='nofollow noopener'> Rapture Of The Nerds</a>
</i> and <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6422238._Makers' title=' Makers' rel='nofollow noopener'> Makers</a>.</i> He is a Fellow for the Elec</span>
  <span id="freeText15649677941057071107" style="display:none">Cory Doctorow is a science fiction author, activist, journalist and blogger — the co-editor of <a href="http://www.boingboing.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Boing Boing</a> and the author of the YA graphic novel <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20575446._In_Real_Life" title=" In Real Life" rel="nofollow noopener"> In Real Life</a>,</i> the nonfiction business book <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20763766._Information_Doesn_t_Want_To_Be_Free" title=" Information Doesn’t Want To Be Free" rel="nofollow noopener"> Information Doesn’t Want To Be Free</a>,</i> and young adult novels like <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6278041._Homeland" title=" Homeland" rel="nofollow noopener"> Homeland</a>,</i> <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13539171._Pirate_Cinema" title=" Pirate Cinema" rel="nofollow noopener"> Pirate Cinema</a>,</i> and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/954674._Little_Brother" title=" Little Brother" rel="nofollow noopener"> Little Brother</a>
</i> and novels for adults like <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13538762._Rapture_Of_The_Nerds" title=" Rapture Of The Nerds" rel="nofollow noopener"> Rapture Of The Nerds</a>
</i> and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6422238._Makers" title=" Makers" rel="nofollow noopener"> Makers</a>.</i> He is a Fellow for the Electronic Frontier Foundation and co-founded the UK Open Rights Group. Born in Toronto, Canada, he now lives in Los Angeles.</span>
